# Cherry-pick revert of Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) fusions (#168157)

**Repository:** pytorch
**Difficulty:** HARD
**Category:** cross_module_bug_fix



## Description

This is a cherry-pick of the revert of PR #168157, which added `Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation` pattern replacement in the Inductor lowering pass.

PR #168157 introduced pattern matching in the Inductor compiler to fuse activation functions (ReLU, GELU) with Addmm (matrix multiply + bias add) operations into a single `_addmm_activation` call that leverages cuBLASLt's fused epilogue support. This optimization aimed to reduce kernel launches and memory traffic for common `Linear -> Activation` patterns.

However, the fusion caused regressions in certain model configurations and needed to be reverted. This cherry-pick applies the revert to the release branch, undoing:
- The `_addmm_activation` pattern replacement in Inductor's lowering/decomposition passes
- The associated pattern matcher registrations for ReLU(Addmm) and GELU(Addmm)
- Any cuBLASLt epilogue fusion paths added for these patterns

Changes:
- 4 files modified
- 93 additions, 87 deletions

## Task

Implement the fix: Cherry-pick revert of Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) fusions

Description: Revert PR #168157 which added `Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation` pattern replacement in the Inductor lowering pass for cuBLASLt fused epilogue support. The fusion caused regressions and needs to be reverted.

   773→def reorder_for_locality(graph: torch.fx.Graph):
   774→    if torch.distributed.is_available():
   775→
   776→        def check():
   777→            # This is a wait node, and `other_node`` is some collective node.
   778→            # Eager semantics allow waits to be issued in a different order than
   779→            # the collectives. Reordering this wait node might reorder collectives
   780→            # which cause hangs. Once we have SPMD mode, we can safely reorder them.
   781→            # However, increasing the locality between a collective and its wait node
   782→            # is generally worse for performance.
   783→            return node.target != torch.ops._c10d_functional.wait_tensor.default

# This makefile does nothing but delegating the actual building to cmake.

SHELL        = /bin/bash
.SHELLFLAGS := -eu -o pipefail -c
PYTHON      ?= $(shell command -v python3 || command -v python)
PIP          = $(PYTHON) -m pip
NIGHTLY_TOOL_OPTS := pull

.PHONY: all
all:
	@cmake -S . -B build $(shell $(PYTHON) ./scripts/get_python_cmake_flags.py) && \
		cmake --build build --parallel --

.PHONY: triton
triton:
	$(PIP) uninstall -y triton
	@./scripts/install_triton_wheel.sh

.PHONY: clean
clean: # This will remove ALL build folders.
	@rm -r build*/ || true

.PHONY: linecount
linecount:
	@cloc --read-lang-def=caffe.cloc caffe2 || \
		echo "Cloc is not available on the machine. You can install cloc with " && \
		echo "    sudo apt-get install cloc"

.PHONY: ensure-branch-clean
ensure-branch-clean:
	@if [ -n "$(shell git status --porcelain)" ]; then \
		echo "Please commit or stash all changes before running this script"; \
		exit 1; \
	fi

.PHONY: setup-env
setup-env: ensure-branch-clean
	$(PYTHON) tools/nightly.py $(NIGHTLY_TOOL_OPTS)

.PHONY: setup-env-cuda
setup-env-cuda:
	$(MAKE) setup-env PYTHON="$(PYTHON)" NIGHTLY_TOOL_OPTS="$(NIGHTLY_TOOL_OPTS) --cuda"

.PHONY: setup-env-rocm
setup-env-rocm:
	$(MAKE) setup-env PYTHON="$(PYTHON)" NIGHTLY_TOOL_OPTS="$(NIGHTLY_TOOL_OPTS) --rocm"

.PHONY: setup-lint
setup-lint .lintbin/.lintrunner.sha256: requirements.txt pyproject.toml .lintrunner.toml
	@echo "Setting up lintrunner..."
	$(PIP) install lintrunner
	lintrunner init
	@echo "Generating .lintrunner.sha256..."
	@mkdir -p .lintbin
	@sha256sum requirements.txt pyproject.toml .lintrunner.toml > .lintbin/.lintrunner.sha256

.PHONY: lazy-setup-lint
lazy-setup-lint: .lintbin/.lintrunner.sha256
	@if [ ! -x "$(shell command -v lintrunner)" ]; then \
		$(MAKE) setup-lint

I have successfully completed the cherry-pick revert of PR #168157. Here's a summary of the changes made:

## Summary of Changes

The following changes were made to revert PR #168157 which added `Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation` pattern replacement in the Inductor lowering pass:

### 1. `torch/_inductor/fx_passes/post_grad.py`
- Removed the `gen_register_replacement` import
- Removed the entire `register_addmm_activation_fusions()` function (lines 684-741)
- Removed the call to `register_addmm_activation_fusions()` in `lazy_init()`

### 2. `test/inductor/test_pattern_matcher.py`
- Removed the `test_addmm_activation_fusion` test method (lines 1219-1281)
- Reverted `test_addmm_alpha_beta_with_pointwise` - changed `torch.abs` back to `torch.nn.functional.relu` in the test functions

### 3. Deleted Files
- `torch/_inductor/fx_passes/serialized_patterns/addmm_gelu_pattern.py`
- `torch/_inductor/fx_passes/serialized_patterns/addmm_relu_pattern.py`

### 4. `torchgen/fuse/gen_patterns.py`
- Removed `post_grad` from the import statement
- Removed the call to `post_grad.lazy_init()`

All Python files pass syntax validation, and the `make test` command returns successfully (with "Nothing to be done" as expected since there's no explicit test target defined).

\"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is a cpu scalar tensor.\n        \"\"\"\n        device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        is_cpu = device is not None and device.type == \"cpu\"\n        ten Otherwise, all dependent\n        constructor nodes won't be moved.\n\n        - target: target device type\n        - allow_outputs: allow outputs to be moved\n        - allow_inputs: allow inputs to be moved\n        \"\"\"\n\n        self.target = target\n        self.allow_inputs = allow_inputs\n        self.allow_outputs = allow_outputs\n\n        assert isinstance(target, str), (\n            \"target should be a string representing the device type. \"\n            f\"Got: {type(target).__name__}\"\n        )\n\n    def allow_cpu_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n           torch.ops.aten.index_put.default,\n            torch.ops.aten.index_put_.default,\n            torch.ops.aten.copy.default,\n            torch.ops.aten.copy_.default,\n            torch.ops.aten.slice_scatter.default,\n        )\n\n    def is_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        node_device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        return node_device is not None and node_device.type == self.target\n\n    def is_cpu_scalar_tensor(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is a cpu scalar tensor.\n        \"\"\"\n        device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        is_cpu = device is not None and device.type == \"cpu\"\n        ten = node.meta.get(\"val\")\n        is_scalar = isinstance(ten, torch.Tensor) and len(ten.size()) == 0\n        return is_cpu and is_scalar\n\n    def all_inputs_are_cpu_scalar_or_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node's inputs are either cpu scalar tensors or\n        on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        inputs = (\n            inp\n            for inp in itertools.chain(node.args, node.kwargs.values())\n            if isinstance(inp, fx.Node)\n        )\n        return all(\n            self.is_cpu_scalar_tensor(inp) or self.is_on_target_device(inp)\n            for inp in inputs\n        )\n\n    def cannot_be_moved(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node can be moved to the target device.\n\n        If this function returns False, it means that this node and all of its users\n        won't be moved into the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        if node.target == \"output\":\n            return not self.allow_outputs\n\n        if not (\n            isinstance(node.target, torch._ops.OpOverload)\n            and node.target.namespace in (\"prims\", \"aten\")\n        ):\n            return True\n\n        if is_index_put_and_requires_h2d_sync_for_gpu_value(node):\n            return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def get_node_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> torch.device | None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Get the device of a node.\n        \"\"\"\n        ten = node.meta.get(\"val\")\n        return None if not isinstance(ten, torch.Tensor) else ten.device\n\n    def get_cpu_indeg_count(self, graph: fx.Graph) -> dict[fx.Node, int]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Get the number of cpu inputs to a node\n        \"\"\"\n        cpu_indeg: dict[fx.Node, int] = Counter()\n\n        for node in graph.nodes:\n            cpu_count = 0\n\n            def add_cpu_inp(node):\n                nonlocal cpu_count\n                device = self.get_node_device(node)\n                cpu_count += device is not None and device.type == \"cpu\"\n\n            pytree.tree_map_only(fx.Node, add_cpu_inp, (node.args, node.kwargs))\n\n            # pyrefly: ignore [redundant-condition]\n            if cpu_count:\n                cpu_indeg[node] = cpu_count\n\n        return cpu_indeg\n\n    def __call__(self, graph: fx.Graph) -> None:\n        target_devices = OrderedSet[torch.device]()\n        constructors = []\n        cpu_placeholders: OrderedSet[fx.Node] = OrderedSet()\n\n        for node in graph.nodes:\n            device = self.get_node_device(node)\n            if device and device.type == self.target:\n                target_devices.add(device)\n\n            if (\n                self.allow_inputs\n                and node.op == \"placeholder\"\n                and self.is_cpu_scalar_tensor(node)\n            ):\n                cpu_placeholders.add(node)\n                constructors.append(node)\n                continue\n\n            if not (\n                isinstance(node.target, torch._ops.OpOverload)\n                and node.target.namespace in (\"prims\", \"aten\")\n            ):\n                continue\n\n            if not torch._subclasses.fake_tensor._is_tensor_constructor(node.target):\n                continue\n\n            if node.kwargs.get(\"device\") != torch.device(\"cpu\"):\n                continue\n\n            constructors.append(node)\n\n        # not handling multiple target devices initially\n        if not constructors or len(target_devices) != 1:\n            return\n\n        movable_constructors = self.find_movable_constructors(graph, constructors)\n\n        target_device = next(iter(target_devices))\n        movable_cpu_placeholders = graph.call_function(torch.ops.aten.unsqueeze.default, (elem, 0))\n                    )\n                    last_node = unsqueezed_nodes[-1]\n            with graph.inserting_after(last_node):\n gpu_node,\n                        lambda x: x\n                        not in [cpu_concat, gpu_concat, gpu_split, gpu_node]\n                        + unsqueezed_nodes\n                        and which constructors cannot be moved to gpu\n        cannot_move_to_gpu = OrderedSet[fx.Node]()\n\n        # For any node in the graph, which constructors does it have a dependency on\n        constructor_dependencies: dict[fx.Node, OrderedSet[fx.Node]] = defaultdict(\n            OrderedSet\n        )\n\n        # if a cpu node has a dependency on two different cpu constructors,\n        # then if either constructor cannot be moved to gpu, the other cannot as well.\n        # In this case any node with a dependency on one will have a dependency on the other\n        equal_constructor_sets: dict[fx.Node, OrderedSet[fx.Node]] = {\n            c: OrderedSet([c]) for c in constructors\n        }\n\n        def make_dependencies_equivalent(\n            set1: OrderedSet[fx.Node], set2: OrderedSet[fx.Node]\n        ) -> OrderedSet[fx.Node]:\n            # could use union find but not worth complexity here\n            set1.update(set2)\n            for obj in set1:\n                equal_constructor_sets[obj] = set1\n            return set1\n\n        queue: list[fx.Node] = list(constructors)\n\n        for c in queue:\n            constructor_dependencies[c].add(c)\n\n        while queue:\n            node = queue.pop()\n            dependencies = constructor_dependencies[node]\n\n            for user in node.users:\n                if self.cannot_be_moved(user):\n                    cannot_move_to_gpu.update(dependencies)\n                    break\n\n                # this node was used on a op which takes in multiple devices and output a gpu\n                # tensor. we can convert its cpu input to gpu without making further changes\n                if self.allow_cpu_device(user) and self.is_on_target_device(user):\n                    del cpu_indeg[user]\n                elif (\n                    self.allow_inputs\n                    and self.all_inputs_are_cpu_scalar_or_on_target_device(user)\n                ):\n                    # Iterable\n\n        import torch\n        from torch._inductor.pattern_matcher import (\n            fwd_only,\n            PatternMatcherPass,\n            register_replacement,\n        )\n\n        def pattern1(x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n            return x + 1\n\n        def replacement1(x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n            return x - 1\n\n        def pattern2(x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n            return x + 2\n\n        def replacement2(x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n            return x - 2\n\n        patterns = PatternMatcherPass()\n        inputs = [torch.empty(4, 5, dtype=torch.float32, device=GPU_TYPE)]\n        register_replacement(pattern1, replacement1, inputs, fwd_only, patterns)\n        register_replacement(pattern2, replacement2, inputs, fwd_only, patterns)\n\n        count = 0\n\n        def custom_pass(graph: torch.fx.Graph):\n            nonlocal count\n            count = patterns.apply(graph)\n\n        def custom_backend(\n            graph: torch.fx.GraphModule, example_inputs: Iterable[torch.Tensor]\n        ) -> Callable:\n            from torch._inductor import config\n\n            current_config = config.shallow_copy_dict()\n            from torch._inductor.compile_fx import compile_fx\n\n            current_config[\"post_grad_custom_post_pass\"] = custom_pass\n            return compile_fx(graph, example_inputs, config_patches=current_config)\n\n        @torch.compile(backend=custom_backend)\n        def f(x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n            y = x + 1\n            y2 = y.relu() + 2\n            return y2\n\n        def f_replaced(x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n            y = x - 1\n            y2 = y.relu() - 2\n            return y2\n\n        inp = torch.rand(3, 5, device=GPU_TYPE)\n        self.assertEqual(f(inp), f_replaced(inp))\n        self.assertEqual(count, 2)\n\n    @skipCUDAIf(not SM80OrLater, \"need sm_80\")\n test_symint_pattern_matching(self):\n        import torch._inductor.config as config\n        from torch._inductor.pattern_matcher import (\n            fwd_only,\n            PatternMatcherPass,\n            register_replacement,\n        )\n\n        saved_graph = None\n\n        class _CustomPass(PatternMatcherPass):\n            def __init__(self) -> None:\n                super().__init__()\n\n            def __call__(self, g: torch.fx.graph.Graph):\n                self.apply(g)\n                nonlocal saved_graph\n                saved_graph = g\n\n        with config.patch(\n            # leave custom pass only in post_grad_passes()\n            pattern_matcher=False,\n            # define pattern match as custom post grad opt pass\n            post_grad_custom_pre_pass=None,\n            post_grad_custom_post_pass=_CustomPass(),\n        ):\n\n            def add(x, y):\n                return x + y\n\n            # testing that\n            def sym_minus(x, y):\n                return (x - (-y.size(0))) - (y * -1) - y.size(0)\n\n            device = \"cpu\"\n            my_args = [\n                torch.empty([8, 1], device=device),\n                torch.empty([10], device=device),\n            ]\n\n            invoked = False\n\n            def extra_check(match):\n                nonlocal invoked\n                invoked = True\n                return True\n\n            register_replacement(\n                add,\n                sym_minus,\n                my_args,\n                fwd_only,\n @functools.cache
def register_addmm_activation_fusions():
    def is_valid_addmm_activation_fusion(match: Match) -> bool:
        # Exclude ROCm
        if torch.version.hip:
            return False

        if config.max_autotune or config.max_autotune_gemm:
            return False

        inp = match.kwargs["inp"].meta["val"]

        if not inp.is_cuda:
            return False

        output = match.output_node()
        return not all(
            is_pointwise_use(use, lambda target: torch.Tag.reduction in target.tags)
            for use in output.users
        )

    args = [torch.empty(3), torch.empty(4, 2), torch.empty(2, 3)]
    beta_alpha_workaround = {"beta": 1.3, "alpha": 1.2}

    def addmm_relu_pattern(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten.relu(aten.addmm(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha))

    def addmm_gelu_pattern(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten.gelu(
            aten.addmm(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha), approximate="tanh"
        )

    def addmm_relu_replacement(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten._addmm_activation(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha)

    def addmm_gelu_replacement(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten._addmm_activation(
            inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha, use_gelu=True
        )

    patterns = (addmm_relu_pattern, addmm_gelu_pattern)
    replacements = (addmm_relu_replacement, addmm_gelu_replacement)
    for pattern, replacement in zip(patterns, replacements):
        key = f"{pattern.__name__}"
        gen_register_replacement(
            key,
            # pyrefly: ignore [bad-argument-type]
            pattern,
            # pyrefly: ignore [bad-argument-type]
            replacement
... (truncated)

    @skipIfRocm
    def test_addmm_activation_fusion(self):
        """
        Test whether Activation(Addmm) implies _addmm_activation
        """

        b = torch.rand(4, device=GPU_TYPE)
        m1 = torch.rand(3, 2, device=GPU_TYPE)
        m2 = torch.rand(2, 4, device=GPU_TYPE)
        alphas = ({"alpha": 0.8}, {})  # **{} -> alpha=1
        betas = ({"beta": 1}, {})  # **{} -> beta=1

        # Cases Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation
        fusable_activations = (
            torch.nn.functional.relu,
            # NOTE: only approximate="tanh" is fusable
            lambda *args, **kwargs: torch.nn.functional.gelu(
                *args, approximate="tanh", **kwargs
            ),
        )
        for activation in fusable_activations:

            def f(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
                return activation(torch.addmm(b, m1, m2, **beta, **alpha))

            fc = torch.compile(f)

            for beta, alpha in itertools.product(betas, alphas):
                expected = f(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha)
                actual = fc(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha)
                torch.testing.assert_close(expected, actual)

                _, (code) = run_and_get_code(fc, b, m1, m2, beta, alpha)
                self.assertIn("_addmm_activation", code[0])

            # Check no disruptions in the gemm autotune process
            _, (code) = run_and_get_code(
                torch.compile(f, options={"max_autotune_gemm": True}),
                b,
                m1,
                m2,
                beta,
                alpha,
            )
            self.assertNotIn("_addmm_activation", code[

    def test_addmm_alpha_beta_with_pointwise(self):
        # Test that addmm with alpha/beta != 1 is unfused correctly with pointwise ops
        # See https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/167313
        x = torch.rand(2, device=GPU_TYPE)
        a = torch.rand(2, 3, device=GPU_TYPE)
        b = torch.rand(3, 2, device=GPU_TYPE)

        def f(x, a, b):
            return torch.nn.functional.relu(torch.addmm(x, a, b, alpha=0.8, beta=0.2))
